    • Array__Dynamic 
      struct Array__Dynamic {
    own mut data : U8
    cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a zero-initialized Array with the given capacity.
    func new(shallow cap: USize) returns Array__Dynamic
    func len(self: Array__Dynamic) returns shallow USize
    /// Unchecked element access: ref to the element at index `i` with
    /// NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`. This is the
    /// unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it directly because
    /// its `_fi < len()` termination test already proves the index in
    /// bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Array__Dynamic, i: USize) returns ref Dynamic
    /// Ref to the element at index `i`. Throws OutOfBounds if `i` is
    /// past the end; call as `arr.get(i)!` to panic on a bad index.
    func get(self: Array__Dynamic, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Dynamic
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.cap`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(self: Array__Dynamic, shallow i: USize, own val: Dynamic)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. Drops the old value. `val` is
    /// owned. Throws OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as
    /// `arr[i] = val` (or `arr.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(self: Array__Dynamic, shallow i: USize, own val: Dynamic, mut _err_kind: I64)
    func delete(own self: Array__Dynamic, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func clone(self: Array__Dynamic) returns Array__Dynamic
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • Str 
      struct Str {
    own mut c_str : I8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    func len(self: Str) returns shallow USize
    /// Return a ref to byte `i`. Panics if `i` is out of bounds.
    func get(self: Str, i: USize) returns ref I8
    /// Unchecked byte access -- caller must ensure i < self.len().
    func unsafe_get(self: Str, i: USize) returns ref I8
    /// Lexicographic comparison. Returns 0 if equal, negative if a < b,
    /// positive if a > b.
    func cmp(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow I64
    /// Equality with a length-mismatch early-out and a same-buffer
    /// shortcut before the byte compare. Otherwise eq auto-derives from
    /// cmp as `cmp(a,b) == 0`, which memcmps the common prefix even when
    /// the lengths already differ; this rejects the common different-length
    /// case (distinct identifiers) without touching the bytes, and
    /// short-circuits interned / identical buffers.
    func eq(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// Create an empty Str pre-allocated for up to `n` bytes.
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Str
    /// Wrap a NUL-terminated C string as a non-owning Str view (no copy).
    /// The view borrows `s`; the caller keeps ownership of the buffer.
    func from_c_str(s: Dynamic) returns Str
    /// Append `s` to `self`. Panics if `self` is a view/literal or if
    /// capacity is exceeded.
    func push_str(mut self: Str, s: Str)
    /// Deep-copy the string into a new owned Str.
    func clone(val: Str) returns Str
    /// String representation of a Str: a fresh owned copy of itself. Lets
    /// Str satisfy the same `T.to_str(x)` contract as the numeric types, so
    /// generic code (e.g. assert_eq(Str, a, b)) works uniformly.
    func to_str(self: Str) returns Str
    /// Free the backing buffer unless it is borrowed/static. CAP_LIT names a
    /// static literal wrapper, so call_free does not free that wrapper either.
    func delete(own self: Str, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Return a view into `s` from `start` for `n` bytes (no allocation).
    /// Clamps to valid bounds.
    func substr(s: Str, shallow start: USize, shallow n: USize) returns Str
    /// Return a view of `s` with leading ASCII whitespace (space, tab,
    /// newline, carriage return) removed. View-only -- no allocation.
    func trim_start(s: Str) returns Str
    /// Return a view of `s` with leading and trailing ASCII whitespace
    /// removed. View-only -- no allocation.
    func trim(s: Str) returns Str
    /// True if `a` contains `b` as a substring.
    func contains(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// True if `a` starts with prefix `b`.
    func starts_with(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// True if `a` ends with suffix `b`.
    func ends_with(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// True if the string has zero length.
    func is_empty(self: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// Return the byte index of the first occurrence of `needle`, or -1.
    func find(self: Str, needle: Str) returns shallow I64
    /// Return the byte index of the last occurrence of `needle`, or -1.
    func rfind(self: Str, needle: Str) returns shallow I64
    /// Return a new Str with all occurrences of `from` replaced by `to`.
    func replace(self: Str, from: Str, to: Str) returns Str
    /// View of the single byte at index `i` as a Str.
    func get_char(self: Str, shallow i: USize) returns Str
    /// Hash via the caller-supplied byte hasher, feeding it the
    /// string CONTENT bytes (c_str + count). The default bytewise
    /// fallback would hash the {c_str, count, cap} struct itself --
    /// i.e. the heap pointer's address -- which is identity, not
    /// equality. The container chooses the algorithm; this method
    /// chooses the right bytes for a Str.
    func hash(self: Str, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    /// If self starts with `prefix`, return the rest; otherwise clone.
    func strip_prefix(self: Str, prefix: Str) returns Str
    /// If self ends with `suffix`, return the part before it; otherwise clone.
    func strip_suffix(self: Str, suffix: Str) returns Str
    /// Create a 1-byte Str from a U8 value.
    func from_byte(shallow byte: U8) returns Str
    /// Parse the string as a signed integer. Accepts an optional leading
    /// '-', base prefixes 0x/0b/0o (issue #255), and '_' digit separators.
    /// Bare digit runs are base-10. Panics on invalid input.
    func to_i64(self: Str) returns shallow I64
    /// Parse as base-10 unsigned 8-bit integer.
    func to_u8(self: Str) returns shallow U8
    /// Parse as base-10 signed 8-bit integer.
    func to_i8(self: Str) returns shallow I8
    /// Parse as base-10 signed 16-bit integer.
    func to_i16(self: Str) returns shallow I16
    /// Parse as base-10 unsigned 16-bit integer.
    func to_u16(self: Str) returns shallow U16
    /// Parse as base-10 signed 32-bit integer.
    func to_i32(self: Str) returns shallow I32
    /// Parse as base-10 unsigned 32-bit integer.
    func to_u32(self: Str) returns shallow U32
    /// Parse as base-10 unsigned 64-bit integer.
    func to_u64(self: Str) returns shallow U64
    /// Parse as base-10 USize (collection sizes/indices).
    func to_usize(self: Str) returns shallow USize
    /// Parse as a floating-point number. Backed by C strtof: handles
    /// decimal and scientific notation at full precision, so a value
    /// printed by F32.to_repr round-trips exactly back to the same F32.
    /// '_' digit separators (issue #255) are stripped first since strtof
    /// does not accept them.
    func to_f32(self: Str) returns shallow F32
    /// Split the string on `delim`, returning a Vec of Str clones.
    func split(self: Str, delim: Str) returns Vec__Str
    func size() returns shallow USize
    func lt(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    func gt(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    func neq(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    func lte(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
    func gte(a: Str, b: Str) returns shallow Bool
}

    • OutOfBounds 
      struct OutOfBounds {
namespace:
    func clone(_self: OutOfBounds) returns OutOfBounds
    func delete(own self: OutOfBounds, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func hash(self: OutOfBounds, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    func eq(_self: OutOfBounds, _other: OutOfBounds) returns shallow Bool
    func to_str(_self: OutOfBounds) returns Str
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    func eq(_self: KeyNotFound, _other: KeyNotFound) returns shallow Bool
    func to_str(_self: KeyNotFound) returns Str
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    cap : USize

    /// Create a zero-initialized Array with the given capacity.
    func new(shallow cap: USize) returns Array__Str
    func len(self: Array__Str) returns shallow USize

    /// NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`. This is the

    • Vec__Str 
      struct Vec__Str {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__Str
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Str
    func len(self: Vec__Str) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__Str)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__Str, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__Str, own val: Str)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__Str, own other: Vec__Str)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__Str, mut other: Vec__Str)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__Str, i: USize) returns ref Str
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__Str, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Str
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__Str) returns Str
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__Str, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Str
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__Str, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__Str, shallow i: USize, own val: Str)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__Str, shallow i: USize, own val: Str, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__Str, mut src: Vec__Str, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__Str, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__Str) returns Vec__Str
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • U8 
      struct U8 {
namespace:
    ext_func to_i64(shallow val: U8) returns shallow I64
    ext_func to_i32(shallow val: U8) returns shallow I32
    ext_func to_usize(shallow val: U8) returns shallow USize
    ext_func to_f32(shallow val: U8) returns shallow F32
    /// Convert to decimal string representation.
    func to_str(shallow val: U8) returns Str
    core_func add(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func sub(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func mul(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func div(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func mod(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func inc(mut self: U8)
    core_func dec(mut self: U8)
    /// Return the multiplicative identity (1) for this type.
    func unity(shallow _self: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func eq(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow Bool
    core_func neq(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow Bool
    core_func lt(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow Bool
    core_func gt(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow Bool
    core_func lte(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow Bool
    core_func gte(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow Bool
    ext_func cmp(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow I64
    core_func band(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func bor(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func bxor(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func bnot(shallow a: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func shl(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    core_func shr(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8) returns shallow U8
    ext_func clone(val: U8) returns shallow U8
    /// Absolute difference between two values, useful for Range iteration.
    func distance(a: Dynamic, b: Dynamic) returns shallow U64
    func delete(own self: U8, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func size() returns shallow USize
    /// Addition that throws IntegerOverflow on unsigned wrap.
    /// Use U8.add for the wrapping variant.
    func safe_add(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8, mut _err_kind: I64, mut _err_IntegerOverflow: IntegerOverflow, loc: Str) returns shallow U8
    /// Subtraction that throws IntegerOverflow when a < b (underflow
    /// wraps unsigned). Use U8.sub for the wrapping variant.
    func safe_sub(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8, mut _err_kind: I64, mut _err_IntegerOverflow: IntegerOverflow, loc: Str) returns shallow U8
    /// Multiplication that throws IntegerOverflow on unsigned wrap.
    /// Use U8.mul for the wrapping variant.
    func safe_mul(shallow a: U8, shallow b: U8, mut _err_kind: I64, mut _err_IntegerOverflow: IntegerOverflow, loc: Str) returns shallow U8
    /// Minimum representable value.
    MIN : U8
    /// Maximum representable value.
    MAX : U8
    func hash(shallow self: U8, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
}

    • Array__Bool 
      struct Array__Bool {
    own mut data : U8
    cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a zero-initialized Array with the given capacity.
    func new(shallow cap: USize) returns Array__Bool
    func len(self: Array__Bool) returns shallow USize
    /// Unchecked element access: ref to the element at index `i` with
    /// NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`. This is the
    /// unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it directly because
    /// its `_fi < len()` termination test already proves the index in
    /// bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Array__Bool, i: USize) returns ref Bool
    /// Ref to the element at index `i`. Throws OutOfBounds if `i` is
    /// past the end; call as `arr.get(i)!` to panic on a bad index.
    func get(self: Array__Bool, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Bool
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.cap`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(self: Array__Bool, shallow i: USize, own val: Bool)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. Drops the old value. `val` is
    /// owned. Throws OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as
    /// `arr[i] = val` (or `arr.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(self: Array__Bool, shallow i: USize, own val: Bool, mut _err_kind: I64)
    func delete(own self: Array__Bool, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func clone(self: Array__Bool) returns Array__Bool
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • Expr 
      struct Expr {
    mut node_type : NodeType
    mut children : Vec__Expr
    mut line : U32
    mut col : U32
namespace:
    /// Null-safe delete. The auto-generated version dereferences `self`
    /// unconditionally, so the asap pass deleting an owned-but-null Expr
    /// (e.g. a fold helper that returns NULL on failure) SEGVs. Guarding
    /// here lets functions return owned `Expr` that may be null without
    /// the caller having to clone-and-leak to dodge the deep delete.
    func delete(own self: Expr, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Print a diagnostic error with file path and source location.
    proc error(self: Expr, path: Str, msg: Str)
    /// Like error() but adds "not implemented yet" note.
    proc todo_error(self: Expr, path: Str, msg: Str)
    /// Like error() but adds "bug in the language" note.
    proc lang_error(self: Expr, path: Str, msg: Str)
    /// Take ownership of `child` and append it to the children list.
    func add_child(mut self: Expr, own child: Expr)
    /// Clone `child` and append the clone to the children list.
    func push_child_clone(mut self: Expr, child: Expr)
    /// Append other's children into self via raw memcpy (no cloning).
    /// Zeroes other's count so it no longer owns the moved items.
    func take_children(mut self: Expr, mut other: Expr)
    /// Create a new Expr with the given node_type and source location.
    func new(data: NodeType, shallow line: U32, shallow col: U32) returns Expr
    func eq(_self: Expr, _other: Expr) returns shallow Bool
    func til_type(self: Expr) returns Type
    func set_til_type(mut self: Expr, shallow t: Type)
    func to_str_indent(self: Expr, shallow indent: U32) returns Str
    func to_str(self: Expr) returns Str
    func clone(self: Expr) returns Expr
    func hash(self: Expr, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
    • Map__I64_Str

    /// Drop all live keys and values but keep the allocated storage so the Map can be reused.

    /// `key` is absent; call as `map.get(k)!` (or `map[k]`) to panic
    /// on a missing key.

    /// Insert or overwrite the value for `key`. The value is owned.

    • Vec__Bool 
      struct Vec__Bool {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__Bool
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Bool
    func len(self: Vec__Bool) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__Bool)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__Bool, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__Bool, own val: Bool)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__Bool, own other: Vec__Bool)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__Bool, mut other: Vec__Bool)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__Bool, i: USize) returns ref Bool
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__Bool, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Bool
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__Bool) returns shallow Bool
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__Bool, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Bool
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__Bool, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__Bool, shallow i: USize, own val: Bool)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__Bool, shallow i: USize, own val: Bool, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__Bool, mut src: Vec__Bool, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__Bool, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__Bool) returns Vec__Bool
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__I64, i: USize) returns ref I64
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__I64, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref I64
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__I64) returns shallow I64
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__I64, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__I64
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__I64, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__I64, shallow i: USize, own val: I64)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__I64, shallow i: USize, own val: I64, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__I64, mut src: Vec__I64, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__I64, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__I64) returns Vec__I64
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
    • Vec__FieldLayout 
      struct Vec__FieldLayout {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__FieldLayout
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FieldLayout
    func len(self: Vec__FieldLayout) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, own val: FieldLayout)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, own other: Vec__FieldLayout)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, mut other: Vec__FieldLayout)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__FieldLayout, i: USize) returns ref FieldLayout
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__FieldLayout, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref FieldLayout
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout) returns FieldLayout
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FieldLayout
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, shallow i: USize, own val: FieldLayout)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, shallow i: USize, own val: FieldLayout, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__FieldLayout, mut src: Vec__FieldLayout, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__FieldLayout, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__FieldLayout) returns Vec__FieldLayout
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__Tuple, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__Tuple, own val: Tuple)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__Tuple, own other: Vec__Tuple)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__Tuple, mut other: Vec__Tuple)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__Tuple, i: USize) returns ref Tuple
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__Tuple, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Tuple
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__Tuple) returns Tuple
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__Tuple, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Tuple
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__Tuple, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__Tuple, shallow i: USize, own val: Tuple)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__Tuple, shallow i: USize, own val: Tuple, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__Tuple, mut src: Vec__Tuple, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__Tuple, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__Tuple) returns Vec__Tuple
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

      struct Range {
    start : U64
    end : U64
namespace:
    /// Create a Range from `start` (inclusive) to `end` (exclusive).
    func new(shallow start: U64, shallow end: U64) returns Range
    func len(self: Range) returns shallow U64
    /// The i-th value in the range (start+i or start-i for reverse).
    func get(self: Range, shallow i: U64) returns shallow U64
    func clone(val: Range) returns Range
    func delete(own self: Range, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func hash(self: Range, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    func eq(self: Range, other: Range) returns shallow Bool
    func to_str(self: Range) returns Str
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • File 
      struct File {
    ref mut handle : U8
    mut is_write : Bool
    mut is_update : Bool
namespace:
    ext_proc readfile(path: Str) returns Str
    ext_proc writefile(path: Str, content: Str)
    /// Open a file at `path` for reading or writing.
    func new(path: Str, shallow is_write: Bool) returns File
    /// Open a file at `path` for in-place update: reads and writes are
    /// both allowed and the cursor can be moved with `seek`, so small
    /// regions can be patched without rewriting the whole file. The file
    /// must already exist.
    func update(path: Str) returns File
    /// Write a string to the file and return `self` so writes chain via
    /// UFCS: `f.write("a").write("b").write("c")`. Panics unless opened
    /// for writing or update.
    proc write(self: File, s: Str) returns ref File
    /// Read the entire file contents into a Str. Panics if opened
    /// write-only.
    func read_all(self: File) returns Str
    /// Read up to `count` bytes starting at the current cursor position
    /// and advance the cursor. The result is shorter than `count` near
    /// end-of-file. Panics if opened write-only.
    func read(self: File, shallow count: I64) returns Str
    /// Return the current cursor position as a byte offset from the start
    /// of the file.
    func tell(self: File) returns shallow I64
    /// Move the cursor to an absolute byte offset from the start of the
    /// file. Returns `self` so calls chain via UFCS.
    proc seek(self: File, pos: I64) returns ref File
    /// Move the cursor by `delta` bytes relative to its current position
    /// (`delta` may be negative). Returns `self` so calls chain via UFCS.
    proc seek_cur(self: File, delta: I64) returns ref File
    /// Move the cursor to `delta` bytes relative to the end of the file
    /// (`delta` is typically <= 0). `f.seek_end(0)` followed by `f.tell()`
    /// yields the file size. Returns `self` so calls chain via UFCS.
    proc seek_end(self: File, delta: I64) returns ref File
    /// Close the underlying file handle and NULL it. Private: invoked
    /// only from `delete`, which the garbager inserts after a File
    /// local's last use.
    func close(mut self: File)
    /// Release the File: close the handle, then free the struct shell
    /// unless the caller still owns it (`call_free = false` for a
    /// stack/value local). The garbager inserts this call right after the
    /// File's last use.
    func delete(own self: File, shallow call_free: Bool)
    proc fwrite(self: File, parts: ..Str) returns ref File
    func clone(self: File) returns File
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

      struct Map__Str_TokenType {
    mut keys : Vec__Str
    mut values : Vec__TokenType

    /// The key type must implement `cmp`.

    /// Drop all live keys and values but keep the allocated storage so the Map can be reused.

    • Vec__Token 
      struct Vec__Token {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__Token
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Token
    func len(self: Vec__Token) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__Token)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__Token, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__Token, own val: Token)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__Token, own other: Vec__Token)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__Token, mut other: Vec__Token)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__Token, i: USize) returns ref Token
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__Token, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Token
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__Token) returns Token
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__Token, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Token
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__Token, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__Token, shallow i: USize, own val: Token)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__Token, shallow i: USize, own val: Token, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__Token, mut src: Vec__Token, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__Token, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__Token) returns Vec__Token
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
    • Vec__TokenType

    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__TokenType, i: USize) returns ref TokenType

    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__TokenType) returns TokenType
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__TokenType, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__TokenType
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__TokenType, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__TokenType, shallow i: USize, own val: TokenType)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__TokenType, shallow i: USize, own val: TokenType, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__TokenType, mut src: Vec__TokenType, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__TokenType, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__TokenType) returns Vec__TokenType
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • Vec__Dynamic 
      struct Vec__Dynamic {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__Dynamic
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Dynamic
    func len(self: Vec__Dynamic) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__Dynamic)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, own val: Dynamic)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, own other: Vec__Dynamic)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, mut other: Vec__Dynamic)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__Dynamic, i: USize) returns ref Dynamic
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__Dynamic, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Dynamic
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__Dynamic) returns Dynamic
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__Dynamic
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, shallow i: USize, own val: Dynamic)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, shallow i: USize, own val: Dynamic, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__Dynamic, mut src: Vec__Dynamic, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__Dynamic, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__Dynamic) returns Vec__Dynamic
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • Vec__FFITypePtrBox 
      struct Vec__FFITypePtrBox {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__FFITypePtrBox
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FFITypePtrBox
    func len(self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, own val: FFITypePtrBox)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, own other: Vec__FFITypePtrBox)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, mut other: Vec__FFITypePtrBox)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, i: USize) returns ref FFITypePtrBox
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref FFITypePtrBox
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox) returns FFITypePtrBox
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FFITypePtrBox
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, shallow i: USize, own val: FFITypePtrBox)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, shallow i: USize, own val: FFITypePtrBox, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, mut src: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__FFITypePtrBox) returns Vec__FFITypePtrBox
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__FuncType
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FuncType
    func len(self: Vec__FuncType) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__FuncType)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__FuncType, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__FuncType, own val: FuncType)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__FuncType, own other: Vec__FuncType)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__FuncType, mut other: Vec__FuncType)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__FuncType, i: USize) returns ref FuncType
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__FuncType, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref FuncType
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__FuncType) returns FuncType
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__FuncType, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FuncType
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__FuncType, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__FuncType, shallow i: USize, own val: FuncType)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__FuncType, shallow i: USize, own val: FuncType, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__FuncType, mut src: Vec__FuncType, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__FuncType, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__FuncType) returns Vec__FuncType
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__FFIEntry, i: USize) returns ref FFIEntry
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__FFIEntry, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref FFIEntry
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__FFIEntry) returns FFIEntry
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__FFIEntry, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__FFIEntry
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__FFIEntry, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__FFIEntry, shallow i: USize, own val: FFIEntry)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__FFIEntry, shallow i: USize, own val: FFIEntry, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__FFIEntry, mut src: Vec__FFIEntry, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__FFIEntry, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__FFIEntry) returns Vec__FFIEntry
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
    • Vec__ExprPtrBox 
      struct Vec__ExprPtrBox {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__ExprPtrBox
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__ExprPtrBox
    func len(self: Vec__ExprPtrBox) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, own val: ExprPtrBox)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, own other: Vec__ExprPtrBox)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, mut other: Vec__ExprPtrBox)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, i: USize) returns ref ExprPtrBox
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref ExprPtrBox
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox) returns ExprPtrBox
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__ExprPtrBox
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, shallow n: USize)

    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, shallow i: USize, own val: ExprPtrBox)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, shallow i: USize, own val: ExprPtrBox, mut _err_kind: I64)

    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same

    func delete(own self: Vec__ExprPtrBox, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__ExprPtrBox) returns Vec__ExprPtrBox
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

      struct Map__Str_I64 {
    mut keys : Vec__Str
    mut values : Vec__I64
namespace:
    /// Create an empty Map of the types provided for the key and values respectively.
    /// The key type must implement `cmp`.
    func new() returns Map__Str_I64
    func len(self: Map__Str_I64) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live keys and values but keep the allocated storage so the Map can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Map__Str_I64)
    /// True if a value exists for the given key.
    func has(self: Map__Str_I64, key: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// Return a ref to the value for `key`. Throws KeyNotFound if

    /// Insert or overwrite the value for `key`. The value is owned.
    func set(mut self: Map__Str_I64, key: Str, own val: I64)
    func delete(own self: Map__Str_I64, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func clone(self: Map__Str_I64) returns Map__Str_I64
    func hash(self: Map__Str_I64, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__CoverageNode, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__CoverageNode, shallow i: USize, own val: priv___src_self_typer_til__CoverageNode)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__CoverageNode, shallow i: USize, own val: priv___src_self_typer_til__CoverageNode, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__CoverageNode, mut src: Vec__CoverageNode, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__CoverageNode, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__CoverageNode) returns Vec__CoverageNode
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

      struct Map__Str_DeclRef {
    mut keys : Vec__Str
    mut values : Vec__DeclRef
namespace:
    /// Create an empty Map of the types provided for the key and values respectively.
    /// The key type must implement `cmp`.
    func new() returns Map__Str_DeclRef
    func len(self: Map__Str_DeclRef) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live keys and values but keep the allocated storage so the Map can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Map__Str_DeclRef)
    /// True if a value exists for the given key.
    func has(self: Map__Str_DeclRef, key: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// Return a ref to the value for `key`. Throws KeyNotFound if
    /// `key` is absent; call as `map.get(k)!` (or `map[k]`) to panic
    /// on a missing key.
    func get(self: Map__Str_DeclRef, key: Str, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref priv___src_self_loader_til__DeclRef
    /// Insert or overwrite the value for `key`. The value is owned.
    func set(mut self: Map__Str_DeclRef, key: Str, own val: priv___src_self_loader_til__DeclRef)
    func delete(own self: Map__Str_DeclRef, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func clone(self: Map__Str_DeclRef) returns Map__Str_DeclRef
    func hash(self: Map__Str_DeclRef, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
    • Vec__ProgramUnit 
      struct Vec__ProgramUnit {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__ProgramUnit
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__ProgramUnit
    func len(self: Vec__ProgramUnit) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, own val: ProgramUnit)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, own other: Vec__ProgramUnit)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, mut other: Vec__ProgramUnit)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__ProgramUnit, i: USize) returns ref ProgramUnit
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__ProgramUnit, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref ProgramUnit
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit) returns ProgramUnit
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__ProgramUnit
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, shallow i: USize, own val: ProgramUnit)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, shallow i: USize, own val: ProgramUnit, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__ProgramUnit, mut src: Vec__ProgramUnit, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__ProgramUnit, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__ProgramUnit) returns Vec__ProgramUnit
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
