    • Vec__LocalInfo 
      struct Vec__LocalInfo {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__LocalInfo
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__LocalInfo
    func len(self: Vec__LocalInfo) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, own val: priv___src_self_garbager_til__LocalInfo)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, own other: Vec__LocalInfo)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, mut other: Vec__LocalInfo)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__LocalInfo, i: USize) returns ref priv___src_self_garbager_til__LocalInfo
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__LocalInfo, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref priv___src_self_garbager_til__LocalInfo
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo) returns priv___src_self_garbager_til__LocalInfo
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__LocalInfo
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, shallow i: USize, own val: priv___src_self_garbager_til__LocalInfo)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, shallow i: USize, own val: priv___src_self_garbager_til__LocalInfo, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__LocalInfo, mut src: Vec__LocalInfo, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__LocalInfo, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__LocalInfo) returns Vec__LocalInfo
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__DocEntry, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__DocEntry, shallow i: USize, own val: DocEntry)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__DocEntry, shallow i: USize, own val: DocEntry, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__DocEntry, mut src: Vec__DocEntry, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__DocEntry, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__DocEntry) returns Vec__DocEntry
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

      struct Map__Str_Binding {
    mut keys : Vec__Str
    mut values : Vec__Binding
namespace:
    /// Create an empty Map of the types provided for the key and values respectively.
    /// The key type must implement `cmp`.
    func new() returns Map__Str_Binding
    func len(self: Map__Str_Binding) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live keys and values but keep the allocated storage so the Map can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Map__Str_Binding)
    /// True if a value exists for the given key.
    func has(self: Map__Str_Binding, key: Str) returns shallow Bool
    /// Return a ref to the value for `key`. Throws KeyNotFound if
    /// `key` is absent; call as `map.get(k)!` (or `map[k]`) to panic
    /// on a missing key.
    func get(self: Map__Str_Binding, key: Str, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref Binding
    /// Insert or overwrite the value for `key`. The value is owned.
    func set(mut self: Map__Str_Binding, key: Str, own val: Binding)
    func delete(own self: Map__Str_Binding, shallow call_free: Bool)
    func clone(self: Map__Str_Binding) returns Map__Str_Binding
    func hash(self: Map__Str_Binding, hasher: HashFn) returns shallow U64
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    • Vec__DynPtrBox 
      struct Vec__DynPtrBox {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__DynPtrBox
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__DynPtrBox
    func len(self: Vec__DynPtrBox) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, own val: priv___src_self_interpreter_til__DynPtrBox)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, own other: Vec__DynPtrBox)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, mut other: Vec__DynPtrBox)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__DynPtrBox, i: USize) returns ref priv___src_self_interpreter_til__DynPtrBox
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__DynPtrBox, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref priv___src_self_interpreter_til__DynPtrBox
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox) returns priv___src_self_interpreter_til__DynPtrBox
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__DynPtrBox
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, shallow i: USize, own val: priv___src_self_interpreter_til__DynPtrBox)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, shallow i: USize, own val: priv___src_self_interpreter_til__DynPtrBox, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__DynPtrBox, mut src: Vec__DynPtrBox, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__DynPtrBox, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__DynPtrBox) returns Vec__DynPtrBox
    func size() returns shallow USize
}

    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__Binding, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__Binding, shallow i: USize, own val: Binding)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__Binding, shallow i: USize, own val: Binding, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__Binding, mut src: Vec__Binding, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__Binding, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__Binding) returns Vec__Binding
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
    • Vec__HeapBinding 
      struct Vec__HeapBinding {
    own mut data : U8
    mut count : USize
    mut cap : USize
namespace:
    /// Create a new empty Vec for elements of type T.
    func new() returns Vec__HeapBinding
    /// Create an empty Vec pre-sized for `n` elements, so pushing up to `n`
    /// items reallocs zero times. Use at call sites where the final length is
    /// known up front (cloning a Vec of known length, building a fixed arg
    /// list, ...) to avoid the 1->2->4->...->n grow-and-realloc churn that
    /// `new()` + repeated `push` pays. cap is clamped to >= 1 so the doubling
    /// in push/append never starts from zero (n=0 behaves like new()).
    func with_capacity(shallow n: USize) returns Vec__HeapBinding
    func len(self: Vec__HeapBinding) returns shallow USize
    /// Drop all live elements via elem_delete but keep the allocated
    /// storage and element-type metadata so the Vec can be reused.
    func clear(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding)
    /// Drop the elements flagged in `marks` (a byte-per-element buffer,
    /// nonzero = drop, at least self.count entries) via elem_delete, then
    /// compact the survivors forward and update count. This is the
    /// container home for the scavenger's mark/sweep/compact, which used
    /// to reach into data/count directly.
    func delete_marked(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, marks: Dynamic)
    /// Append an element to the end. `val` is owned: after this call the
    /// caller must not use the value passed -- clone it first if needed.
    func push(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, own val: HeapBinding)
    /// Consume the contents of `other` by appending them to `self`.
    /// `other` is taken by ownership and will be empty after the call.
    func append(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, own other: Vec__HeapBinding)
    /// Replace self's contents with other's via memcpy (no per-elem clone).
    /// Avoids the Vec_clone + extra Vec_delete that plain `self = other` emits.
    /// Takes `mut` (not `own`) so caller retains ownership of other; its
    /// natural scope-end auto-delete frees other.data. Setting other.count = 0
    /// prevents that auto-delete from re-running elem_delete on items whose
    /// bytes were moved into self.
    func move_from(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, mut other: Vec__HeapBinding)
    /// Unchecked element access: return a reference to the element at
    /// index `i` with NO bounds check. The caller must prove `i < len()`.
    /// This is the unchecked core that `get` wraps; for-in uses it
    /// directly because its `_fi < len()` termination test already
    /// proves the index in bounds (issue #284).
    func unsafe_get(self: Vec__HeapBinding, i: USize) returns ref HeapBinding
    /// Return a reference to the element at index `i`. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i]`
    /// to panic on a bad index. The reference is valid until the
    /// next mutation.
    func get(self: Vec__HeapBinding, i: USize, mut _err_kind: I64) returns ref HeapBinding
    /// Remove and return the last element. Panics if empty. The caller
    /// takes ownership of the returned value.
    func pop(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding) returns HeapBinding
    /// Split off the first `n` elements into a new Vec. Panics if `n`
    /// exceeds self.len(). The remaining elements shift to the front.
    func take_prefix(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, shallow n: USize) returns Vec__HeapBinding
    /// Drop the elements from index `n` to the end, freeing each via
    /// elem_delete, and set count to `n` (the survivors [0, n) are left
    /// untouched). Panics if `n` exceeds len. This is the container home
    /// for a pop-and-free-the-tail loop shrinking a Vec back to a mark.
    func truncate(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, shallow n: USize)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i` without a bounds check, dropping
    /// the old value. Caller guarantees `i < self.count`; the write-side
    /// mirror of unsafe_get (issue #284).
    func unsafe_set(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, shallow i: USize, own val: HeapBinding)
    /// Overwrite the element at index `i`. `val` is owned. Throws
    /// OutOfBounds if `i` is past the end; call as `vec[i] = val`
    /// (or `vec.set(i, own val)!`) to panic on a bad index.
    func set(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, shallow i: USize, own val: HeapBinding, mut _err_kind: I64)
    /// Move bytes of src[i] into self (push). Source slot is zeroed so that
    /// src's eventual elem_delete on it is a no-op (relies on the same
    /// count==0/data==NULL convention used by take_children and Vec.delete).
    func push_take(mut self: Vec__HeapBinding, mut src: Vec__HeapBinding, shallow i: USize)
    /// Drop each element via elem_delete, free storage, then free self
    /// unless `call_free` is false.
    func delete(own self: Vec__HeapBinding, shallow call_free: Bool)
    /// Deep-copy the Vec and all its elements via elem_clone.
    func clone(self: Vec__HeapBinding) returns Vec__HeapBinding
    func size() returns shallow USize
}
